
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Calculate the volume of tetrahedron ABCD using the given edge lengths.'}, {'objective': 'Calculate the total surface area of tetrahedron ABCD by finding the area of each triangular face.'}, {'objective': 'Use the formula relating volume, surface area, and inradius to find the equal distance from point I to each face.'}, {'objective': 'Express the distance in the form (m√n)/p with positive integers m, n, p and find m+n+p.'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- The geometric object is a tetrahedron named ABCD.
- Edge lengths are given as follows:
  AB = CD = √41,
  AC = BD = √80,
  BC = AD = √89.
- There exists a point I inside the tetrahedron such that the perpendicular distances from I to each of the four faces are equal.
- The common distance from I to each face can be expressed in the form (m√n)/p, where m, n, p are positive integers, m and p are coprime, and n is square-free.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The tetrahedron has pairs of edges equal in length, suggesting some symmetry or special configuration.
- The equal distances from point I to all faces imply that I is the incenter of the tetrahedron (the point equidistant from all faces).
- The given edge lengths impose constraints on the shape and size of the tetrahedron, affecting the position of I and the value of the inradius.
- The problem’s structure relies on geometric properties of tetrahedra, such as face areas, volumes, and distances from points to planes.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- The problem lies primarily in Euclidean geometry, specifically 3D geometry involving tetrahedra.
- Concepts involved include spatial distances, properties of polyhedra, and possibly vector or coordinate geometry.
- Such problems are common in mathematical competitions and advanced geometry studies.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The exact coordinates or spatial orientation of the tetrahedron are not given, only edge lengths.
- It is assumed that the tetrahedron is non-degenerate and that the point I lies strictly inside.
- Computing the incenter and inradius from edge lengths alone can be complex, requiring careful handling of face areas and volume.
- The problem assumes uniqueness of point I, which is typical for the incenter but not explicitly stated.
- Potential challenges include verifying the tetrahedron’s existence with given edges and calculating the inradius without explicit coordinates.

        "Given solutions to the problem from other agents, consider their opinions as additional advice. Please think carefully and provide an updated answer."

    all_answer1 = [[] for _ in range(N_max_1)]

        "subtask_id": "subtask_1",
        "instruction": debate_instr,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "Debate"
    }

            if r == 0:

                input_infos_1 = [taskInfo] + all_thinking1[r-1]
                thinking1, answer1 = await agent(input_infos_1, debate_instr, r, is_sub_task=True)
